[Atharvan.тАФsaptatis tryadhik─Б, yamadevatyam mantroktabahudevatyaс╣Б ca (5, 6. ─Бgneyy─Бu, 44, 46. mantroktadevatye; 50. bh─Бum─л; 54. ─Бindav─л; 56. ─Бpy─Б). tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 4, 8, 11, 23. sataс╕еpan╠Дkti; 5. 3-p. nicс╣Ыd g─Бyatr─л; 6, 56, 68, 70, 72. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 18, 25-29, 44, 46. jagat─л (18. bhurij; 29. vir─Бj)*; 30. 5-p. atijagat─л; 31. vir─Бс╣н ┼Ыakvar─л; 32-35, 47, 49, 52. bhurij; 36. 1-av. ─Бsury anuс╣гс╣нubh; 37. 1-av. ─Бsur─л g─Бyatr─л; 39. par─Бtriс╣гс╣нup pan╠Дkti; 50. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti; 54. puro тАШnuс╣гс╣нubh; 58. vir─Бj; 60. 3-av. 6-p. jagat─л; 64. bhurik pathy─Бpan╠Дkty ─Бrс╣г─л; 67. pathy─Б bс╣Ыhat─л; 69, 71. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л.]

Griffith

A funeral hymn, taken partly from the Rigveda

режрез рдЗрдпрдВ рдирд╛рд░реАрдкрддрд┐рд▓реЛрдХрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This woman, choosing her husband’s world, lies down (ni-pad) by
    thee that art departed, O mortal, continuing to keep [her] ancient
    duty (dh├бrma); to her assign thou here progeny and property.
Notes

Verses 1-4 are translated and interpreted (I think, incorrectly) by
Hillebrandt in ZDMG. xl. 708 ff. K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 44) and the comm. declare
that with this verse the wife is made to lie down beside her dead
husband on the funeral pile. The comm. glosses dharm─Бm with sukс╣Ыtam,
and understands the sense of the p─Бda as it is translated above. The
sense of d alone seems to indicate that the woman’s action is
nothing more than a show, expected to be followed by that of the next
verse, since “progeny and property” are rewards for this life, not for
the other. The comm. says it is meant for her next birth. TA. also has
the verse (in vi. 1. 3), but reads for c v├н┼Ыvam pur─Бс╣З├бm ├бnu
p─Бl├бyant─лтАФa very inferior text. Some of our mss. (O.Op.D.R.K.), and
even the majority of SPP’s, have in c -p─Бd├бyant─л, but SPP. rightly
accepts -p─Бl├б-; тМКc.f. the phonetic relation of udumbara and
ulumbala, above, 2. 13тМЛ.

Griffith

Choosing her husband’s world, O man, this woman lays herself down beside thy lifeless body. Preserving faithfully the ancient custom. Bestow upon here both wealth and offspring.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go up, O woman, to the world of the living; thou liest by (upa-┼Ы─л)
    this one who is deceased: come! to him who grasps thy hand, thy second
    spouse (didhiс╣г├║), thou hast now entered into the relation of wife to
    husband.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 18. 8, whose text differs only by reading in c
didhiс╣г├│s, and this is given also by two of our mss. (R.D.) and the
majority of SPP’s, so that it certainly ought to be accepted as the true
reading, dadh- being only a corruption. TA. (in vi. 1. 3) has
didhiс╣г├│s, but after it tv├бm et├бt, and in b it─Б╠Бsum, in neither
case making any important change in the sense. тМКTA., both text and comm.
in both ed’s, reads abh├н s├бmbabh┼лva: the comm. renders by
─Бbhimukhyena samyak pr─Бpnuhi! which procedure gives a shock even to
one who is wonted to the Hindu laxity of ideas about v─Бiyadhikaraс╣Зya.тМЛ
The meaning given to abh├н s├бm-bh┼л in the translation is decidedly the
only admissible one; nor need one hesitate to render didhiс╣г├║ according
to its later accepted meaning. The woman cannot be left free and
independent; she can only be relieved of her former wifehood by taking
up a new one (even if this be, as is probable enough, nominal only); he
who grasps her hand to lead her down from the pile becomes, at least for
the nonce, her husband. The direction of K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 45) in connection
with the verse is simply “one makes her rise”; the comm. тМКvol. iv., p.
129, endтМЛ specifies that this is done “if she desires to live in this
world again”; neither tells who is to take her handтАФas, for example,
─А┼Ыval─Бyana does (AGS. iv. 2. 18): “her husband’s brother, a
representative of her husband, a pupil [of her husband], or an aged
servant.” тМКWhether the levir and the “representative” are the same
person or two different ones does not appear from the translation nor
from the original of AGS.тМЛ V─Бit. (38. 3) uses the verse in the
puruс╣гamedha.

Griffith

Rise, come unto the world of life, O woman: come, he is lifeless by whose side thou liest. Wifehood with this thy husband was thy portion who took thy hand and wooed thee as a lover.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I saw the maiden being led, being led about, alive, for the dead; as
    she was enclosed with blind darkness, then I led her off-ward (├бp─Бc─л)
    from in front (pr─Бkt├бs).

Griffith

I looked and saw the youthful dame escorted, the living to the dead: I saw them, bear her. When she with blinding darkness was enveloped, then did I turn her back and lead her homeward.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдореН) рдЬреАрд╡рддреА рд╣реБрдИ [рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердпреБрдХреНрдд] (рдпреБрд╡рддрд┐рдореН) рдпреБрд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА (рдиреАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд▓реЗ рдЬрд╛рдпреА рдЧрдпреА рдФрд░ (рдореГрддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ)рдорд░реЗ рд╣реБрдУрдВ рд╕реЗ [рдореГрддрдХ рд╡рд╛ рдорд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдЧрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ] (рдкрд░рд┐рдгреАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдкреГрдердХреН рд▓реЗ рдЬрд╛рдпреА рдЧрдпреА (рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрдореН) рдореИрдВрдиреЗ рджреЗрдЦреА рд╣реИред (рдпрддреН) рдХреНрдпреЛрдВрдХрд┐ рд╡рд╣ (рдЕрдиреНрдзреЗрди рддрдорд╕рд╛) рдЧрд╣рд░реЗ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ [рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рди рди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд╢реЛрдХ рд╕реЗ] (рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡реГрддрд╛) рдврдХреА рд╣реБрдИ (рдЖрд╕реАрддреН) рдереА, (рддрддреН) рдЗрд╕реА рд╕реЗ (рдПрдирд╛рдореН) рдЙрд╕ (рдЕрдкрд╛рдЪреАрдореН) рдЕрд▓рдЧ рдкрдбрд╝реА рд╣реБрдИ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреНрддрдГ) рд╕рд╛рдордиреЗ (рдЕрдирдпрдореН) рдореИрдВрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ реерейрее

Translation
  1. Foreknowing, O inviolable one, the world of the living, moving
    together [with him] upon the road of the godsтАФthis is thy herdsman
    (g├│pati); enjoy him; make him ascend to the heavenly (svarg├б) world.
Notes

There is no difficulty in understanding this of the anustaraс╣З─л cow,
with the s┼лtras and commentaries, although we should expect rather
pitс╣Ыlok├бm in a, and joс╣гaya in c. тМКBy “s┼лtras” I suppose W.
means s┼лtra 20 of K─Бu┼Ы. 81 (cited under vs. 3) and s┼лtra 37 of K─Бu┼Ы.
80 (cited under this vs.); and by “commentaries,” the AV. comm. to vss.
3-4 (vol. iv., p. 131┬│) and the comm. to the TA. correspondent in vi.
12. 1 (Poona ed., p. 449) of our vs. 3.тМЛ Besides the use of the verse
with the one preceding, as explained under the latter, it again (K─Бu┼Ы.
80. 37) accompanies the leading of a cow around fuel and fire; and the
schol. (note to 81. 33) employ it further at the kindling of the pile.
The verse lacks only one syllable of being a regular triс╣гс╣нubh (11 +
11: 10 + 11 = 43).

Griffith

Knowing the world of living beings, Aghnya! treading the path. of Gods which lies before thee, This is thy husband: joyfully receive him and let him mount into the world of Svarga.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unto sky (div), unto reed, more helpful of streams; O Agni, gall of
    the waters art thou.
Notes

The translation of a and b is purely mechanical. Other texts
have a quite different version of them. VS. (xvii. 6 a-c) reads ├║pa
jm├бnn ├║pa vetas├й тАЩvatara nad─л╠Бс╣гv ─Б╠Б; MS. (in ii. 10. 1; but p.
├бvataram) the same (and the editor reports K. and Kap.S. as agreeing);
TS. (in iv. 6. 1┬▓) the same except ├бvattaram; VS. and MS. admit a much
more intelligible rendering (‘close to earth, close to reeds, descend
thou in the streams’). In all the other texts, the verse is preceded by
our vi. 106. 3 a, b and other similar addresses to Agni, in the
agnicayana ceremony; and so also in V─Бit. (29. 13), where the verses
accompany the drawing of a frog, of the water-plant avak─Б, and of
reeds, across the fire-site in all directions. In K─Б├║┼Ы. (82. 26), this
verse and 3. 60 are used in. the ceremony of gathering the bone-relics
on the third day after cremation, with the direction iti mantrokt─Бny
avad─Бya. тМКThe authorities differ as to the day: Caland,
Todtengebr├дuche, p. 99.тМЛ The comm. explains тМКvol. iv., p. 132┬╣тБ╡, p.
169┬▓тБ░тМЛ that vss. 5 and 6 тМК(cf. Ath. Paddhati cited in note to K─Бu┼Ы. 82.
26)тМЛ тМКand 60тМЛ are addressed to the plants mentioned in those verses тМКand
gives a list of plants: cf. SPP’s note with extract from Ke┼Ыava, and
Bloomfield’s note to 82. 26тМЛ. The comm. adds that the plants are used by
the performer in besprinkling a Brahman’s bones with milk. Under this
verse the comm. makes dy─Бm mean avak─Бm, because this rises above the
water without touching earth! The verse does not need to be scanned as
nicс╣Ыt.

Griffith

The speed of rivers craving heaven and cane, thou, Agni, art the waters’ gall.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Whom thou, O Agni, didst consume, him do thou extinguish again;, let
    there grow here the ky─Б╠Бmb┼л, the ┼Ы─Бс╣Зс╕Нad┼лrv─Б╠Б, the vy├аlka┼Ы─Б.
Notes

RV. (x. 16. 13) has the same verse, but calls two of the plants
kiy─Б╠Бmbu and p─Бkad┼лrv─Б╠Б. Vy├аlka┼Ы─Б (p. v├нре░alka┼Ы─Б) might well be an
adjective, ‘free from alka┼Ыa’ or the like, if we only knew what
alka┼Ыa meant. тМКW’s Op.R. accent vyalka┼Ы─Б╠Б: and so five of SPP’s
authorities, against four with vy├аl-.тМЛ TA. disagrees with both AV. and
RV. in reading at vi. 4. 1 ky─Бmb┼л╠Бs тМКboth ed’sтМЛ, but agrees with RV. in
having p─Бkad┼лrv─Б╠Б, тМКand with both ed’s of AV. in accenting vy├аlka┼Ы─БтМЛ;
it reads j─Бyat─Бm for rohatu in c, and tv├бm for t├бm in
b.тАФThe comm. explains ┼Ы─Бс╣Зс╕Нad┼лrv─Б as d┼лrv─Б (‘millet’) that
springs up near water, having egg-shaped roots, or that has long joints,
and adds that it is called “big millet” (bс╣Ыhadd┼лrv─Б); but this is
probably without authority. With as little reason he glosses alka by
┼Ы─Бkh─Б ‘branch,’ and declares vyalko┼Ыa to mean “furnished with
various (vividha) branches”; тМКso also the comm. on RV. and on TA.тМЛ.
The verse is not directly quoted by K─Бu┼Ы., but (as was pointed out
above) it is regarded by the comm. тМКand the PaddhatiтМЛ as included with
vss. 5 and 60 in 82. 26, and probably with justice.тАФThis verse and its
successor in RV. and TA. (strangely removed to be 3. 60 in AV.) are both
plainly intended as remedial and expiatory for the cruel office of Agni
in burning a corpse; the fire is not only to be extinguished, but to be
followed by its antithesis, the growth of water-plants and the
appearance of their attendant frogs: compare Bloomfield in AJP. xi.
342-350 тМКor JAOS. xv., p. xxxixтМЛ. тМКThis expiatory and remedial rite is
avouched for antiquity by MBh. viii. 20. 50 = 819: P─Бс╣Зс╕Нyaс╕е…svadh─Бm (=
preta┼Ыar─лrar┼лpaс╣Б haviс╕е) iv─Б тАЭpya jvalanaс╕е pitс╣Ыpriyas (= ┼Ыma┼Ы─Бn─Бgniс╕е)
tataс╕е pra┼Ы─Бntaс╕е salilaprav─Бhataс╕е; and a note to the P. C. Roy version
of this passage, p. 65, says that it persists even to this day in
India.тМЛ

Griffith

Cool, Agni, and again refresh the spot which thou hast scorched and burnt. Here let the water-lily grow, and tender grass and leafy plant.

режрен рдЗрджрдВ рддрдПрдХрдореН ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Here is one for thee, beyond is one for thee; enter thou into union
    with the third light; at entrance be thou fair (c─Б╠Бru) with [thy]
    body, loved of the gods in the highest station.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 56. 1, which reads in c tanv├аs, and in d
jan├нtre (for sadh├бsthe). It is also found in SV. (i. 65), TB. (in
iii. 7. 1┬│), TA. (vi. 3. 1; 4. 2), and ─Аp. (ix. i. 17); in a,
TB.┬п─Аp. have u (for ┼л before te); in c, all have saс╣Бv├й┼Ыanas,
while SV. gives tanv├и and the others tan├║v─Бi; in d, TB.─Аp. read
priy├й, and SV.TB.─Аp. agree with RV. in jan├нtre. According to K─Бu┼Ы.
(80. 36), the verse accompanies the carrying of the fire at the head of
the procession to the funeral pile; as the comm. states it, carrying the
three fires, in the case of one who has established sacrificial fires.
The three “lights” are thus understood to be the three sacrificial
fires; but they are probably, in the original meaning of the verse,
rather three regions of light, to the highest of which the deceased is
to be translated.

Griffith

Here is one light for thee, another yonder: enter the third and be therewith united. Uniting with a body be thou lovely, dear to the Gods in their sublimest mansion.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Rise thou, go forth, run forth; make thee a home (├│kas) in the sea
    [as] station; there do thou, in concord with the Fathers, revel with
    soma, with the svadh─Б╠Бs.
Notes

The first half-verse is found also in TA. (in vi. 4. 2) which has the
easier ending param├й vy├▓man; the second half of the TA. verse is our
vi. 63. 3 c, d. The majority of our saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. combine drav├│
тАЩkaс╕е in a-b, but SPP. reports nothing of the kind from his
authorities. The verse can be forced down to forty syllables (as a
pan╠Дkti) by violence in c; тМКits natural scansion is as 8 + 11: 11 +
11тМЛ. It is one of the utth─Бpan─л or ‘uplifting’ verses, which, with the
hariс╣З─лs or ’taking’ verses, are used more than once in K─Бu┼Ы., and are
cited in V─Бit. (37. 23-24) and elsewhere, in connection with lifting and
moving the corpse etc. This one accompanies (K─Бu┼Ы. 80. 31) the raising
of the corpse to carry it to the funeral pile, and later (80. 35), with

  1. 61 and 3. 9 and others, the lifting on to the cart and removing; and
    yet later (82. 31) the gathering up and carrying away the bone-relics.
Griffith

Rise up, advance, run forward: make thy dwelling in water that shall be thy place to rest in There dwelling in accordance with the Fathers delight thyself with Soma and libations.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Start (cyu) forward, collect (sam-bhс╣Ы) thy body; let not thy
    limbs (g─Б╠Бtra) nor thy frame (┼Ы├бr─лra) be left out; enter together
    after thy mind that has entered; wherever in the world thou enjoyest,
    thither go.
Notes

The first half-verse and the last p─Бda are found also, as parts of
different verses, in TA. vi. 4. 2; which, however, reads ├║t tiс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б тАЩtas
tan├║vaс╣Б s├бm bharasva m├й тАЩh├б g─Б╠Бtram ├бva h─Б m─Б╠Б ┼Ы├бr─лram, and y├бtra
bh┼л╠Бmy─Бi vс╣Ыс╣З├бse t├бtra gaccha. Some of our mss. (P.M.O.R.T.K.) accent
├бnu in c; and some (all except O.Op.R.K., also two of SPP’s) have
bh┼л╠Бme in d; the comm. reads bh┼л╠Бm─Бu. According to K─Бu┼Ы. (80. 32),
the dead body, after being raised (utth─Бpay-) with the preceding
verse, is made three times to set forth (? saс╣Бh─Бpay-; sam-h─Б means
usually simply ‘get up’: it is added, “as many times as it is raised”)
with this one; and this verse is used again, with the preceding verse
(under which see) and others, in 80. 35 and 82. 31.

Griffith

Prepare thy body: speed thou on thy journey: let not thy limbs,. thy frame be left behind thee. Follow to its repose thy resting spirit: go to whatever spot of earth thou lovest.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the soma-drinking (somy├б) Fathers anoint me with splendor, the
    gods with honey, with ghee; making me pass further on unto sight, let
    them increase me, attaining old age, unto old age.
Notes

Some of the mss. (including our D.R.p.m.T.) read ├бjantu in b;
possibly it is their way of emending the false accent of ├б├▒jantu;
doubtless we ought to change this to a├▒j├бntu rather than to admit the
modulated stem ├б├▒ja. The prat─лka (varcas─Б m─Бm) applies either to
this verse or to the next, or probably is used to include both; whatever
it applies to is used, according to K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 47; 87. 4), in connection
with rinsing the mouth at the end of the cremation ceremony and at the
beginning of the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a; and also (86. 17), with 3. 61-67, in
the ceremony of interring the bones, in connection with supporting the
dhruvanas* on the north-west of the fire. The comm. takes notice of
only the first of these three applications. *тМКCaland, WZKM. viii. 369,
would read dhuvan─Бny upayachante at 86. 16: I suppose he would render,
’they offer fannings [to the relics].’ But are we sure that 86. 17

Griffith

With splendour may the Fathers, meet for Soma, with mead and. fatness may the Gods anoint me. Lead me on farther to extended vision, and prosper me through life of long duration.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Agni anoint me completely with splendor; let Vishс╣Зu anoint
    wisdom into my mouth; let all the gods fix wealth upon me; let pleasant
    waters purify me with purifiers.
Notes

The verse is, with resolution of m─Б╠Б-am, a regular triс╣гс╣нubh, and no
pan╠Дkti. As to its ritual application, see under the preceding verse;
the comm. regards it as sharing with that verse.

Griffith

May Agni balm me thoroughly with splendour; may Vishnu. touch my lips with understanding. May all the Deities vouchsafe me riches, and pleasant Waters purify and cleanse me.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Mitra-and-Varuс╣Зa have enclosed (pari-dh─Б) me; let the sacrificial
    posts of Aditi increase me; let Indra anoint splendor into my hands; let
    Savitar make me one attaining old age.
Notes

Most of our mss. (all except Op.R.), and half of SPP’s, read at the
beginning m├нtr─Бvaruс╣З─Б (Bp. -с╣З─Бu), vocative, which might stand if we
altered adh─Бt─Бm to -th─Бm; both editions give mitr─Б╠Бv├бruс╣З─Б, ours by
emendation. A variant for sv├бravas in b would be very welcome; the
comm. gets rid of the difficulty in its characteristic way, by making
the word an adjective to ─Бdity─Бs, and signifying either “making a
pleasant sound” or “making a distress directed at our enemies”! The
third p─Бda, if properly read, has a redundant syllable; but the Anukr.
would apparently have us read nyanaktu in three syllables, as written.
The K─Бu┼Ы. uses the verse with washing the hands, at the end of the
cremation ceremony (81. 46), and at the beginning of the
piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a (87. 3); the comm. notices only the latter of the two
uses.

Griffith

Mitra and Varuna have stood about me. Adityas, Sacirifical Posts exalt me! May Indra balm my hands with strength and splendour. A long, long life may Savitar vouchsafe me.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Him who died first of mortals, who went forth first to that world,
    Vivasvant’s son, assembler of people, king Yama honor ye with oblation.
Notes

The second half-verse is identical with 1. 49 c, d, and the first
half is analogous with the same, a, b (= RV. x. 14. 1 etc.: see
under 1. 49). The verse is redundant by a syllable in тМКthe perfectly
good jagat─л p─БdaтМЛ d. For its use by K─Бu┼Ы., with 2. 49, see under
the latter; тМКand especially my note to i. 49тМЛ. тМКThe verse is discussed
by Hillebrandt, Ved. Mythol. i. 491.тМЛ

Griffith

Worship with sacrificial gift King Yama, Vivasvan’s son who gathers men together, Yama who was the first to die of mortals, the first who travelled to the world before us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Go away, ye Fathers, and come; this sacrifice is all anointed with
    honey for you; both give to us here excellent property, and assign to us
    wealth having all heroes.
Notes

The second half-verse is found also in A┼ЫS. (ii. 7. 9) and MB. (ii. 3.
5); both read at the end ni yacchata, and at the beginning MB. has
datt─Б тАЩsm-, and A┼ЫS. strangely datt─Бy─Б тАЩsm-. тМКOur pada-texts read
datt├│ (=datt├б u) ├нti: see Pr─Бt. i. 80.тМЛ The translation implies
that dr├бviс╣Зe тАЩh├б is for dr├бviс╣Зam ih├б (p. dr├бviс╣З─Б: ih├б); the comm.
glosses dr├бviс╣З─Б by draviс╣Зam; тМКcf. my Noun-Inflection, p. 331, ┬╢
4тМЛ. The comm. also understands the first p─Бda to signify that the
Fathers are to go to their own world, and then to return when invoked to
their own sacrifice; and this is probably the sense.

Griffith

Depart, O Fathers, and again come hither; this sacrifice of yours is balmed with sweetness. Enrich us here with gift of great possessions; grant blessed wealth with ample store of heroes.

Translation
  1. Let Kaс╣Зva, Kaksh─лvant, Purum─лс╕Нha, Agastya, ┼Ыy─Бv─Б┼Ыva, Sobhar─л,
    Archan─Бnas, Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra, Jamadagni here, Atri, Ka┼Ыyapa, V─Бmadeva, aid us.
Notes

The comm. amuses himself with giving etymologies for all these names,
only passing over Agastya and Sobhar─л as “evident” (prasiddha).

Griffith

Kanva, Kakshivan, Purumidha, Agastya, Syavasva Sobhari, and Archananas, This Visvamitra, Jamadagni, Atri, Kasyapa, Vamadeva be our helpers!

Translation
  1. O Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra, Jamadagni, Vasishс╣нha, Bharadv─Бja, Gotama,
    V─БmadevaтАФAtri hath taken (grabh) our ┼Ыard├нs with obeisances; ye
    Fathers of good report, be gracious to us.
Notes

The translation implies in d emendation of s├║-saс╣Б┼Ы─Бsas to
su┼Ыaс╣Еsasas тМКso W’s ms.! it must certainly be a double slip for
s├║┼Ыaс╣Еs─БsasтМЛ, for which it seems most probably a corruption, and which
is read by the comm. тМКhe reads in fact su┼Ыaс╣Еs─Бsas, and understands it
as W. doesтМЛ; the only variants in the mss. are s├║┼Ыaс╣Е┼Ы─Бsas тМКwith
palatal ┼Ы twiceтМЛ in some of ours (P.M.I.) and one (C.) of SPP’s, and the
accentuation on the second syllable, -s├бс╣Б┼Ы-, in a few (including our
O.R.T.).* P├нtaras in b ought properly to be without accent. тМКAs
to what precedes, see the next ┬╢.тМЛ Some of the mss. read ┼Ы├бrdir or
┼Ы├бrd├нr. The comm. first identifies the word with chardis, and
pronounces it a name for ‘house’; then, as alternative, he gets it from
root ┼Ыard and makes ┼Ыardayati signify balayati; тМКand, as a final
alternative, he regards the word as the name of a RishiтМЛ. Neither K─Бu┼Ы.
nor V─Бit. makes any use of these two verses. тМКWeber, Episches im

this book xviii. with the K─Бu┼Ыikan Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras.тМЛ

*тМКThe decision here lies between the well-authenticated su-┼Ы├бс╣Еsa (‘of
good wishes, kindly’: root ┼Ыaс╣Еs) and the doubtful su-saс╣Б┼Ы─Бs (‘kindly
admonishing,’ presumably oxytone: root ┼Ы─Бs with sam). The former
occurs five times in RV. and also at AV. xix. 10. 6. The latter occurs
nowhere, unless here, nor does it seem to be apposite in meaning: yet
the authority of the mss. and of the ┼Ыrotriya V. is decidedly in favor
of it. No ms. soever actually gives s├║┼Ыaс╣Еs─Бsas; but the mss. that have
the impossible s├║┼Ыaс╣Е┼Ы─Бsas may well be regarded as intending
s├║┼Ыaс╣Еs─Бsas.тАФMoreover, if the two vocatives stood in the order p├нtaraс╕е
su-, I should leave the second one unaccented (Gram. ┬з314 d), as W.
suggests; but with the order s├║- p├нt-, the second seems distinctly
more independent of the first (Gram. ┬з314 e) and may properly be
accented. I would therefore read s├║┼Ыaс╣Еs─Бс╣гaс╕е p├нtaraс╕е, and render ‘O ye
kindly ones, ye Fathers!’ As for the meaning of su┼Ы├бс╣Еsa: note that
┼Ы├бс╣Еsa means ‘a wish, good or evil,’ i.e. not only ‘curse,’ but also
‘blessing,’ and is used in these two opposite senses in two contiguous

to the Fathers, as at RV. x. 78. 3, pitс╣Эс╣З─Б╠Бс╣Б n├б ┼Ы├бс╣Еs─Бс╕е sur─Бt├бyaс╕е. Note
further that ‘kindly’ accords well with the character of the Fathers as
described in RV. x. 15: they bless and help (vss. 5 d, 4 c), and
are harmless (1 c, 6 c) and gracious (3 a, 9 c).тАФThat,
in such a “pestilent congregation of” sibilants as s├║┼Ыaс╣Еs─Бsas, a
blunder of the tradition is rather to be expected than not, is my
opinion: whoso doubts it, let him attempt “with moderate haste” to
repeat aloud three times the simple English sentence “she sells
sea-shells."тМЛ

Griffith

Vasishtha, Jamadagni, Visvamitra, Gotama, Vamadeva, Bhara- dvaja! Atri hath won your favour with homage. Gracious to us be ye praiseworthy Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They overpass defilement (ripr├б), wiping [it] off in the metal
    bowl (? kasy├б), assuming further on newer life-time, filling
    themselves up with progeny and riches; then may we be of good odor in
    the houses.
Notes

тМКP─Бda c = RV. x. 18. 2 c.тМЛ The translation boldly assumes that
kasy├б is a corruption of, or equivalent to, kaс╣Еs├б; the Pet. Lexx.
pass the word without notice; the comm. says that kasa means k─лkasa
‘vertebra,’ the k─л being dropped by Vedic license (!), and that
kasya, as an adjective derived from it, means “the place of
cremation”! All authorities read kasy├й without variation, тМКsave that
SPP’s ┼Ыrotriya K., whose memory of this book was not perfect, recited
k├бsyeтМЛ. тМКSee note* below.тМЛ The authorities are divided, however,
between mс╣Ыj─Б╠Бn─Бs and mс╣Ы╠Бj─Бn─Бs (among those having the latter are our
O.R.); both editions give the former, though it is an isolated
accentuation; mс╣Ыj─Бn├б is regular (and occurs in RV.), while mс╣Ы╠Бj─Бna is
supported (Gram. ┬з619 d) by the analogy of several other such
participles; тМКcf. note to vs. 73тМЛ. Two of our three pada-mss. (Bp.Kp.)
have ─Бyuс╕ере░d├бdh─Бn─Бs in b as compound, and most of our
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. (all save O.R.) accent accordingly ─Бyur d-; but SPP.
acknowledges the reading in only a single ms. (pada), and of course
gives in his text (as we in ours by emendation) ─Б╠Бyur d-. The comm.
regards surabh├бyas in d as figurative, for ┼Ыl─Бghyaguс╣Зayukt─Бs. In
K─Бu┼Ы. (84. 10) the verse is directed to be used as the women go three
times round (the relics of the funeral pile) leftwise, with disheveled
hair and beating the right thigh.

*тМКAccording to Caland, WZKM. viii. 369, the passage in K─Бu┼Ы. 84. 8-11
describes the curious rite named dhuvana or ‘fanning’ of the
bone-relics: see his Todtengebr├дuche, pages 138-9, and cf. my note to
vs. 10, above. The dhuvana is part of the procedure called nidh─Бna
or ’laying to rest’ (ibidem, p. 129). According to the s┼лtra next
preceding 84. 10, an empty pot, rikta-kumbha, is set down, and beaten
with an old shoe. According to our AV. comm. (p. 143┬╣тБ╖ but see SPP’s
note 5), our verse is repeated by the one who breaks the empty jar,
rikta-kala┼Ыa, on the night of the day of cremation, that is, at a time
a good deal earlier than the nidh─Бna!тАФHowever that may be, it does
seem as if our kasy├й might well mean the same thing as the kumbha or
kala┼Ыa of the ritual authorities.тМЛ

Griffith

They, making for themselves a new existence, wash off defilement in the brazen vessel. May we be fragrant in our houses, ever increasing in our children and our riches.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They anoint, they anoint out (v├н), they anoint together (s├бm);
    they lick the rite (? kr├бtu), they smear (abhi-a├▒j) with honey; the
    bull (ukс╣г├бn) flying in the upheaving of the river, the victim (pa┼Ы├║)
    do the gold-purifiers seize (gс╣Ыh) in them тМКf.тМЛ.
Notes

The verse is RV. ix. 86. 43, the only variant in which is gс╣Ыbhс╣Зate at
the end (and our I. also has this; also the comm.). SV. (i. 564; ii.
964) has it also and agrees with RV. in this word, but also has before
it aps├║ instead of ─Бsu, and in b m├бdhv─Б. The comm. understands
sth─Бl─лс╣гu to be intended by the pronoun ─Бsu. The verse is one of the
wild utterances of the soma-purifiers in RV., and seems to be introduced
here without any proper connection with the funeral ceremonies, simply
because there is so much “anoint” in it. In K─Бu┼Ы. (88. 16), it
accompanies an anointing in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a; and in V─Бit. (10. 4),
a smearing of the sacrificial post with butter in the pa┼Ыubandha.
тМКP─Бdas b, c, d are good jagat─л: but a has no jagat─л
character whatever, and by count it is vir─Бj rather than bhurij; but
perhaps the Anukr. (see note to the excerpts from Anukr.) does not mean
to call it bhurij.

Griffith

They balm him, balm him over, balm him thoroughly, caress the mighty power and balm it with the mead, They seize the flying steer at the stream’s breathing-place: cleansing with gold they grasp the animal herein.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What of you is joyous, O Fathers, and delectable (somy├б),
    therewith be at hand (sac), for ye are of own splendor; do ye, rapid
    (? ├бrvan) poets, listen, beneficent, invoked at the council.
Notes

Nearly all our mss. (save Op.R.s.m.) accent pit├бras in a; SPP.
reports only a single pada-ms. as doing so, and of course reads
pitaras, as does our text by emendation. Nearly all the authorities,
again, give bh┼лt├бm at end of b; тМКbut Whitney’s Op. has bh┼лt─Б╠Б;
and hisтМЛ K. has bh┼лt├б, as have three of SPP’s, who reads bh┼лt├б. тМКThe
word itself is lost from the comm., but glossed by bhavatha.тМЛ We ought
to have emended to bh┼лt├б. Once more, all the authorities without
exception accent suvidatr─Б╠Бs, which SPP. accordingly retains, while we
have made the necessary emendation to -d├бtr─Бs. One is tempted to
change arv─Бс╣Зas in c to arv─Б├▒cas. The extra syllable in b
suggests corruption; тМКand so, perhaps, does the fact that in O.R. the
avas─Бna is before bh┼лt├бm, not after itтМЛ.

Griffith

Fathers, be glorious in yourselves, and follow all that is glad in you and meet for Soma. Give ear and listen, swiftly-moving Sages, benevolent, invoked in our assembly.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ye who are Atris, An╠Дgirases, Navagvas, having sacrificed, attached
    to giving (? r─Бtiс╣г─Б╠Бc), bestowers (d├бdh─Бna), and who are rich in
    sacrificial fees, well-doingтАФdo ye revel, sitting on this barh├нs.
Notes

The meaning of some of these epithets is not altogether clear. No use is
made of the verse in the s┼лtras.

Griffith

Atris, Angirases, Navagvas, givers of liberal gifts, continual sacrificers, Devout and pious, granting guerdon freely, sit on this holy grass and be ye joyful.

Whitney
Translation
  1. So then as our distant Fathers, the ancient ones, O Agni, sharpening
    the rite: they went to the bright, they shone,* тМКshould be shiningтМЛ,
    praising with song; splitting the ground, they uncovered the ruddy ones.
Notes

The verse corresponds to RV. iv. 2. 16, found also in VS. (xix. 69) and
TS. (in ii. 6. 12тБ┤) which read precisely with RV. The variants of our
text are no better than corruptions; the others have at end of b
─Б┼Ыuс╣г─Бс╣З─Б╠Бs тМКp. ─Б┼Ыuс╣г─Бс╣З─Б╠Бс╕етМЛ and in c d─л╠Бdhitim. The translation
follows our text.* The comm. takes ─Б┼Ыa┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бs (p. ─Бре░┼Ыa┼Ы-) from root
a┼Ы, and glosses it with vy─Бpnuvantas! The “ruddy ones” are in its
opinion the dawns тМКor else the stolen cows which the An╠Дgirases got back
from the Paс╣ЗisтМЛ.тАФ*тМКWhitney’s ms. reads “they shone”: this is probably
an oversight and should be “shining”; his Bp., to be sure, but Bp.
alone, has d─л╠Бdhyata, not -taс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

As in the days of old our ancient Fathers, speeding the work of sacred worship, Agni! Sought pure light and devotion, singing praises, they cleft the ground and made red Dawns apparent.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Of good actions, well-shining, pious, heavenly ones (dev├б),
    forging the generations as [smiths forge] metal, brightening Agni,
    increasing Indra, they have made for us a wide conclave (pariс╣г├бd),
    rich in kine.
Notes

The corresponding verse in RV. (iv. 2. 17) combines in a-b
devay├бnt├│ тАШyo, has in c vavс╣Ыdh-, and for d ┼лrv├бс╣Б g├бvyam
pariс╣г├бdanto agman; its pada-text in b reads тМКj├бnima like oursтМЛ.
тМКWeber, Sb. 1896, p. 263-64, takes dev─Б╠Б (j├бnim─Б) as = dev─Б╠Бn─Бm
and the whole verse as a parallel to vs. 23, where the phrase dev─Б╠Бn─Бс╣Б
j├бnim─Б occurs in full.тМЛ

Griffith

Gods, doing holy acts, devout, resplendent, smelting like ore their human generation, Brightening Agni and exalting Indra, they came encompassing the stall of cattle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As herds at food (kс╣г├║m), the formidable one hath looked over
    тМК├бtiтМЛ the cattle, the births of the gods, near by; mortals have
    lamented the urv├б┼Ы─лs, unto the increase of the pious, of the next man.
Notes

The translation is purely mechanical, and sundry of the words in it are
extremely questionable. The verse corresponds to RV. iv. 2. 18, which,
however, reads in a kс╣гum├бti as one word (p. kс╣гuре░m├бti; our p.
kс╣г├║m: ├бti), makes good meter in b by inserting y├бt after
dev─Б╠Бn─Бm, and reads in c m├бrt─Бn─Бm. SPP. reads, with RV. and with
the comm., kс╣гum├бti; this is against nearly all his and our
authorities; тМКthey have kс╣г├║m ├бtiтМЛ; but our O.R. have kс╣гum├бti and Op.
has тМКthe impossibleтМЛ kс╣гum: ├бti тМКwith accentless kс╣гumтМЛ. The
translation implies at the end of b ugr├бs, which SPP. reads, with
about half his authorities and the comm.; of ours, most of the later
ones have it also (Op.D. ugr├бс╕е; O.R.K. ugraс╕е тМКaccentless!тМЛ). The
comm. renders a, b thus: “the mighty one, Agni, looks near by upon
the birth of the gods, Indra etc., as in a noisy (kс╣гumati =
┼Ыabdavati) herd (y┼лth─Б being = y┼лthe) of kine a master sees his
own cattle (pa┼Ыvas)”: or, he says, it is the consuming fire that is
addressed: “O Agni, this sacrificer who is being consumed by thee,
mighty by thy favor, in a noisy cattle-crowd, looks upon the birth of
the gods as upon herds of cattle (pa┼Ыvas); the sense being that the
gods come to light in the neighborhood of him who has gone to the world
of the gods.” This is the kind of help that the commentator gives in a
difficult passage. Urv├б┼Ы─лs is to him the Apsarases, Urva┼Ы─л etc.; and
akс╣Ыpran = akalpayan, which means upabhoktuс╣Б samarth─Б bhavanti.
Ary├бs = sv─Бm─л. The verse can be forced into the compass of forty
syllables (11 + 8: 10 + 11 = 40), as the Anukr. estimates it. *тМКThe RV.
verse has been discussed by Bloomfield, JAOS. xx.┬╣, p. 183. He renders
c, d thus: “Even for mortal men Urva┼Ы─лs ere fashioned for the
production of the noble lower ─Аyu.” He takes akс╣Ыpran as ’there were
formed,’ aor. pass. of kс╣Ыp = kс╕╖p: of. the akalpayan of our comm.
and the kс╕╖pt─Бs of S─Бyaс╣Зa on RV. He explains: Just as Urva┼Ы─л, the
goddess Cloud, produces the celestial fire, so the fire-drills (called
urv├б┼Ы─лs) produce for mortals the terrestrial sacrificial fire (├║para
─Бy├║).

Griffith

Strong One! he marked them, and the gods before them, like herds of cattle in a foodful pasture. There man moaned forth their strong desires, to strengthen even the true; the nearest One, the living.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдиреЗ (рдХреНрд╖реБрдорддрд┐) рдЕрдиреНрди [рдШрд╛рд╕ рдЖрджрд┐] рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдореЗрдВ (рдкрд╢реНрд╡рдГ) рдкрд╢реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ (рдпреВрдерд╛ рдЗрд╡) рдпреВрдереЛрдВрдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рдЬрдирд┐рдо) рдЬрдиреНрдо [рдЬреАрд╡рди] рдХреЛ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕рдореАрдк рд╕реЗ (рдЖ) рд╕рдмрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рдЕрдЦреНрдпрддреН) рджреЗрдЦрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдорд░реНрддрд╛рд╕рдГ) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдиреЗ (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рднреА (рдЙрд░реНрд╡рд╢реАрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рдлреИрд▓реАрд╣реБрдИ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдХреГрдкреНрд░рдиреН) рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛ рд╣реИ, (рдЪрд┐рддреН) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЕрд░реНрдпрдГ) рд╡реИрд╢реНрдп (рдЙрдкрд░рд╕реНрдп)рд╕рдореАрдкрд╕реНрде (рдЖрдпреЛрдГ) рдЖрдпреБ рдХреА (рд╡реГрдзреЗ) рдмрдврд╝рддреА рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ [рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ] реереирейрее

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкреА рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреНрдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдзреНрдпрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рджреЗрдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЧреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЪрд░рддреЗрд╣реБрдП рдкрд╢реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЗрдзрд░-рдЙрдзрд░ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рд░реЛрдХ рдХрд░ рджреЗрдЦрддрд╛ рд░рд╣рддрд╛ рд╣реИред рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдп рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдЖрдк рдХреАрдЙрдиреНрдирддрд┐ рд╕реЛрдЪрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рд╕рдм рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдФрд░ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░ рдХрд░реЗрдВреереирейрее

реирек рдЕрдХрд░реНрдо рддреЗрд╕реНрд╡рдкрд╕реЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. We have made [sacrifices] for thee; we have been very active; the
    illuminating (vi-bh─Б) dawns have shone upon [our] rite (с╣Ыt├б); all
    that is excellent which the gods favor; may we talk big at the council,
    having good heroes.
Notes

The first half-verse is, without variant, RV. iv. 2. 19 a, b; the
second half is, also without variant, RV. ii. 23. 19 c, d (and VS.
xxxiv. 58 c, d). Many of the mss., however, (including our Bs.O.K.)
combine in a-b to abh┼лma rt├бm. The comm. has in b the strange
reading avasvan (voc.: = avanavan or p─Бlaka).

Griffith

We have worked for thee, we have toiled and laboured: bright Dawns have shed their light upon our worship. All that the Gods regard with love is blessed. Loud may we speak, with heroes, in assembly.

рдЕрдХреСрд░реНрдоред рддреЗреТред рд╕реБреТрд╜рдЕрдкреСрд╕рдГред рдЕреТрднреВреТрдореТред рдЛреТрддрдореНред рдЕреТрд╡реТрд╕реНрд░реТрдиреНред рдЙреТрд╖рд╕рдГреСред рд╡рд┐реТрд╜рднрд╛реТрддреАрдГред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реСрдореНред рддрддреНред рднреТрджреНрд░рдореНред рдпрддреНред рдЕрд╡реСрдиреНрддрд┐ред рджреЗреТрд╡рд╛рдГред рдмреГреТрд╣рддреНред рд╡реТрджреЗреТрдореТред рд╡рд┐реТрджрдереЗреСред рд╕реБреТрд╜рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГреСред рей.реирекред

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Indra with the Maruts protect me from the eastern quarter;
    arm-moved [is] the earth, as it were to the sky above; to the
    world-makers, the road-makers, do we sacrifice, whoever of you are here,
    sharing in the oblation of the gods.
Notes

тМКAs for this whole passage, vss. 25-37, see my introductory notes, p.
847, ┬╢ 8, and Caland’s orientation of it in his Todtengebr├дuche, p.
154.тМЛ This is a very curious and obscure refrain (its last two p─Бdas
occur again as refrain of 4. 16-24). In b, b─Бhucy├║t─Б(which ought
to mean ‘by a mover, or a moving, of arms’) is rendered as if it were
b─Бh├║cyut─Б; тМКWeber proposes to emend to -t─Бm;тМЛthe comm. also takes
-cyut─Б as past pass. pple., glossing it by vinirgat─Б, or, in an
alternative explanation, by pr─Бpt─Б: either “proceeded out from the
arms of the givers” or “arrived in the arms of the receivers”; the
allusion being to the giving of land to Brahmans: “as land given
protects in the future (up├бri) the heavenly world which is to be
enjoyed by both parties”! The use by the s┼лtras casts no light upon
the meaning. V─Бit. (22. 3) prescribes the verse for use with an offering
to the Maruts in the agniс╣гс╣нoma ceremony тМКdoubtless on account of the
word marutv─БnтМЛ. In K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 39), this verse alone, so far as appears
тМКbut the comm., p. 152тБ╡, says vss. 25-29тМЛ, is combined with 1. 41-43
etc. to accompany the offerings to Sarasvat─л at the funeral pile; again
(85. 26), vss. 25-37 (the comm. says, 25-35) are used with 2. 24, 26,
etc. in connection with the interment of the bone-relics. тМКThis last use
does indeed perhaps cast light on the passage. The previous s┼лtra, 85.
25, with Caland’s emendation (l.c., p. 154), reads: edam barhir
[xviii. 4. 52] ity asthitas tanuс╣Б yath─Бparu saс╣Бcinoti. I think
his emendation receives support from the AV. comm., who says, at vol.
iv., p. 224тБ╢, edam barliir ity с╣Ыc─Б kule jyeс╣гс╣нho тАШsth─лni yath─Бparu
saс╣Бcinuy─Бt. If we take sam-ci in the sense of ‘assemble’ as used in
the phrase ‘assemble the interchangeable parts of a bicycle or a Waltham
watch,’ our s┼лtra would then mean, ‘while repeating xviii. 4. 52, he
(the dead man’s eldest son) assembles a human figure (tanum), limb by
limb, from the bones (asthi-tas), i.e. he makes such a figure out of
the bones by assembling them.’тАФIf this be right, then we probably have
to infer from the AV. text and from the next s┼лtra, 85. 26, that the
eldest son addresses the deities with vss. 25-29, and does so as
spokesman of his dead father, represented by the prostrate figure of
bones; and that, while uttering vss. 30-35, he addresses his dead
father, but does so as speaking for himself.тАФ-As to forming a human

Pitс╣Ыmedhas┼лtra, i. 10, especially lines 5, 7, 10, 13 of p. 15, ed.

Griffith

From eastward Indra, Lord or Maruts, guard me, as in her arms Earth guards the heaven above us! Those who give room, who made the paths, we worship, you, mid the Gods, who share the gifts we offer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Dhartar the maintainer shall maintain thee aloft, as Savitar the
    light (bh─Бn├║) to the sky above; to the world-makers etc. etc.
Notes

The translation follows the comm. in connecting ┼лrdhv├бm with what
precedes, instead of (as the meter suggests, and as is perhaps rather to
be preferred) with what follows it.* The definition by the Anukr. of
the meter of these five verses is not very acceptable; the refrain of
25-28 has 35 syllables (12: 12 + 11); the prefixed variable part varies
from 12 to 14; 28 has 46 syllables (11 + 12: 12 + 11). тМКCf. note to
excerpts from Anukr., above, p. 847, top.тМЛ

*тМКThere is a clear play of words in dhart─Б dharuс╣Зo dh─Бray─Бt─Бi, not
without conscious reminiscence, perhaps, of the familiar plays in
varaс╣Зo v─Бray─Бt─Бi at x. 3. 5 and vi. 85. 1, and in v─Бr idaс╣Б v─Бray─Бt─Бi
varaс╣З─Бvaty─Бm adhi at iv. 7. 1.тАа Moreover, I think that these
derivatives of root dhс╣Ы make clear reference to dhruv─Б di┼Ы, the
‘fixed direction’ or ‘steadfast region,’ and that ┼лrdhvam makes
similar reference to the ‘upward region.’ Render perhaps: ‘Let the
Steadier, steadying, steady thee [in the steadfast region], as aloft
[that is, in the upward region] Savitar [steadieth or maintaineth]
the light, the sky above.’ Cf. my note, p. 847, ┬╢ 8.тАФтАаCf. xix. 36. 6
d.тМЛ

Griffith

May the strong firm Sustainer bear thee upright, as Savitar bears light above the heaven. Those who give room, who made the paths, we worship, you mid the Gods, whe share the gifts we offer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In the eastern quarter, away from approach (?), do I set thee in
    svadh─Б╠Б; arm-moved etc. etc.
Notes

The phrase pur─Б╠Б samvс╣Ы╠Бtaс╕е is very doubtful; perhaps it means rather,
with the more literal sense of pur─Б╠Б and taking -vс╣Ыt as from root
vс╣Ы, ‘before covering up’ тМКso Caland takes it: Todtengebr├дuche, p.
154-5тМЛ; the comm., with his ordinary heedlessness of accent, makes it a
pple. (as if s├бс╣Бvс╣Ыtas), rendering it “formerly covered up” (p┼лrvaс╣Б
saс╣Бch─Бditaс╕е); or else, he says, pur─Б╠Б is instr. of pur = ┼Ыar─лra
‘body,’ and it means “along with thy body” (sa┼Ыar─лra eva san). K─Бu┼Ы.
(80. 53) uses the verse (doubtless with the five that follow it) in
fixing the body in place on the funeral pile; but he adds in the next
rule that Uparibabhrava prohibits it. The comm. takes no notice of any
such application.

Griffith

Toward the eastward region I supply thee before thou goest homeward, with oblation, as in her arms, etc. (as in stanza 25).

These six verses, 30-35, have the same refrain of 35 syllables as vss.
25-28; and the prefixed part, variable only in its first word, ranges
from 17 to 19 syllables; the definition of the Anukr. is approximately

Griffith

Toward the upmost region I supply thee, before thou goest homeward, with oblation, as in her arms Earth bears the heaven above us. Those who give room, who made the paths, we worship, you, mid the Gods, who share the gifts we offer.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Water-purifying art thou; honey-purifying art thou; wind-purifying
    art thou.
Notes

The comm. regards both these prose verses (yajurmantra) as addressed
to Agni, quoting RV. iv. 58. 3 and vi. 16. 39 to prove the applicability
to him of the epithets in 36. The s┼лtras make no use of them save by
their inclusion in the series 25-37 in K─Бu┼Ы. 85. 26: see above, under
vs. 25. The Anukr., in counting the syllables of 36, restores both the
elided initial a’s.

тМКVerses 38 and 39 are addressed to the oblation-carts. The
rearrangement of the RV. p─Бdas in the AV. text is of such critical
interest that it is worth a little space to exhibit the method to the
eye.тАФThe yuje v─Бm etc. of the RV. seems to be clearly prefatory, and
probably few will deny that the RV. order is the more nearly original,
and that the AV. order and readings are secondary.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Both from here and from yonder let them (du.) aid me.

Griffith

From this side and from that let both assist me. As, speeding, ye have come like two twin sisters, Religious-hearted votaries brought you forward. Knowing your several places be ye seated.

Griffith

Sit near, sit very near beside our Soma: for you I fit the ancient prayer with homage. The praise-song, like a chieftain on his pathway, spreads far and wide. Let all Immortals hear it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Three steps the form (?) ascended, it went (?) after the four-footed
    one (f.) with its course (vrat├б); it matches the song (ark├б) with
    the syllable; in the navel of right it purifies.
Notes

The translation is purely mechanical, the verse being highly obscure,
and its AV. version evidently corrupt. RV. (x. 13. 3) reads in a
p├б├▒ca (for tr─л╠Бс╣Зi) and aroham, in b emi for the absurd
─Бitat (apparently a blundering extension* of ─Бit), at end of c
mima et─Б╠Бm, and in d ├бdhi (our abh├н has to be omitted in
translation) s├бm pun─Бmi. It also has in a rup├бs, which SPP.
admits in his text on the authority of the majority of his mss. and of
the comm. (the latter takes it from root rup, and makes it mean
mс╣Ыtaс╕е puruс╣гaс╕е); some of our later mss. (O.Op.R.D.) also give it,
and it is to be regarded as the preferable reading, if there is such a
thing in this case. In b, SPP. strangely reads in his saс╣Бhit─Б-text
─Бitad vr- and in his pada-text etat, his pada-‘mss. having
etat or ─БitтАФboth, doubtless, by accidental misreadings*; the comm.,
however, gives etat, and makes it qualify vratena, being itself =
etena! For n─Бbh─Бu in d the comm. has yon─Бu. *тМКIf ─Бitat is a
“blundering extension of ─Бit” one does not see why W. calls the
pada-reading ─Бit “an accidental misreading."тАФMeantime, in Oertel’s
edition of JUB., published in JAOS. xvi., we find (i. 48, p. 125-6) sa
h─Бi тАЩvaс╣Б с╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыadh─Б тАЭtm─Бnaс╣Б vikс╣Ыtya, s─Бrdhaс╣Б sam─Бit. tad yat s─Бrdhaс╣Б
sam─Бitat, tat s─Бmnas s─Бmatvam; and (iii. 38, p. 197) t─Б с╣Ыca┼Ы ┼Ыar─лreс╣Зa
mс╣Ыtyur anv─Бitat. tad yat etc. On p. 234, Oertel suggests that we might
regard sam─Бitat and anv─Бitat as due to dittography of the following
tat, “were it not for AV. xviii. 3. 40, anv─Бitat, which is protected
by the meter.” Cf. also Henry, Revue Critique, 1894, no’s 39-40, p.
146.тАФSee also SPP’s full critical notes upon the verse, p. 160. It may
be added that W’s O. gives -pad─лm├бс╣Бnv─Б├нt├бd, and his Op. ├бnu: ─Бit├бt.тМЛ

Griffith

Three paces hath the stake gone up, and followed her, the four- footed, with devout observance. He with the Syllable copies the praise-song; he thoroughly purifies at Order’s centre.

Translation
  1. For the gods he chose death; for his progeny did he not choose
    immortality (amс╣Ы╠Бta)? Brihaspati [as] seer extended the sacrifice;
    Yama left (─Б-ric) his dear self (?).

Griffith

Chose he then, death for Gods to be their portion? Why chose he not for men a life eternal? Brihaspati span sacrifice, the Rishi; and Yama yielded up his own dear body.

Griffith

Thou, Agni Jatavedas, when entreated, didst bear our offerings, having made them fragrant. And give them to the Fathers who consumed them with Svadha. Eat, thou God, the gifts we bring thee.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Sitting in the lap of the ruddy ones (f.), assign ye wealth to your
    mortal worshiper (d─Б┼Ыv─Б╠Бс╣Еs); of that good, O Fathers, present ye to
    your sons; do ye bestow (dh─Б) refreshment here.
Notes

The verse is found, without variant, as RV. x. 15. 7 and VS. xix. 63.
The comm. glosses aruс╣З─лn─Бm in a as aruс╣Зavarс╣З─Бn─Бm m─Бtс╣Эс╣З─Бm,
without further explanation. K─Бu┼Ы. does not quote the verse.

Griffith

Lapped in the bosom of the purple Mornings, give riches to the man who brings oblations. Grant to your sons a portion of that treasure, and, present, give them energy, O Fathers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ye fire-sweetened Fathers, come hither; sit on each seat,
    well-conducting ones; eat on the barh├нs the presented oblations, and
    assign to us wealth having all heroes.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 15. 11 through three p─Бdas, RV. having for d:
├бth─Б ray├нс╣Б s├бrvav─лraс╣Б dadh─Бtana; it also reads att─Б╠Б тМКp. att├бтМЛ in
c; and three other texts (VS. xix. 59; TS. in ii. 6. 12┬▓; MS. in iv.
10. 6) agree throughout with it. The comm., too, gives atta and
dadh─Бtana. The Anukr. does not heed that we need at the end
dadh─Бtana to make a full jagat─л. For the use of the verse by K─Бu┼Ы.,
with 45 and 46 and other verses, see under 1. 51; for its use by V─Бit.,
with 45 and other verses, see under 1. 44 and 51.

Griffith

Fathers whom Agni’s flames have tasted, come ye nigh: in per- fect order take ye each your proper place. Eat sacrificial food presented on the grass: grant riches with a multitude of hero sons.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Called unto [are] our delectable (somy├б) Fathers, to dear
    deposits on the barh├нs; let them come; let them listen here; let them
    bless, let them aid us.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 15. 5, which differs only by omitting the
meter-disturbing nas in a. Other texts (VS. xix. 57; TS. ii. 6.
12┬│; MS. iv. 10. 6) agree with RV.; but TS. combines t├й avantu in
d. тМКOur d recurs at TB. ii. 6. 16┬▓.тМЛ The use of the verse in
K─Бu┼Ы. and V─Бit. is the same as that of vs. 44. The comm. glosses
nidh├нс╣гu by nidh─лyam─Бneс╣гu haviс╕ес╣гu.

Griffith

May they, the Fathers who deserve the Soma, invited to their favourite oblations. Laid on the sacred grass, come nigh and listen. May they be gracious unto us and bless us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They who, our father’s fathers, who [his] grandfathers, followed
    after (? anu-h─Б) the soma-drinking, best onesтАФwith them let Yama,
    sharing his gift of oblations, he eager with them eager, eat at
    pleasure.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 15. 8 (and VS. xix. 51, which has the same text with
RV.); this, however, reads for a: y├й naс╕е p┼л╠Бrve pit├бraс╕е somy─Б╠Бsaс╕е.
In b our text gives, with RV. VS. an┼лhir├й (RV. p. anuре░┼лhir├й),
but it is by emendation, for all our mss. have anujahir├й or
an┼лjahir├й, p. anuре░jah─лr├й; тМКthe actual details seem to be as follows:
anujahir├й is given by Bp.P.D., while O.Op.R. have anujah─лr├й; and
an┼лjahir├й is given by Bs.M.T., while K. has an┼лjah─лr├й.тМЛ тМКSPP’s
authorities show the same four varying forms of the word:тМЛ he reads
an┼лjahir├й, p. anuре░jahir├й, although the majority тМКfiveтМЛ of his
saс╣Бhit─Б-authorities and the comm. have the preferable anujah- тМКas
against three with an┼лjah-тМЛ. Our translation implies the manuscript
reading, though it is plainly a corruption of what RV. gives. тМКWhether
we read anujahir├й (from anu-h─Б) or an┼лhir├й (from anu-vah:
S─Бyaс╣Зa, ─Бnup┼лrvyeс╣Зa…dattavantaс╕е; Mah─лdhara, anuvahanti; Weber,
‘welche nachgezogen sind’), in either case the sense is about the same.тМЛ
The comm. treats the word as if it came from root hс╣Ы: anukrameс╣Зa
haranty ─Бtmas─Бt kurvanti. It looks a little as if the text-makers had
in mind the root jeh, found in the next verse. The use of the verse
with its two predecessors in K─Бu┼Ы. was noted under vs. 44. It is very
unsuitably reckoned by the Anukr. a jagat─л, having only one real
jagat─л p─Бda; тМКit scans perfectly as 12 + 11: 11 + 11; the corruption
anujahire gives b 12 syllables, but no true jagat─л characterтМЛ.
тМКW’s version of c accords with Geldner’s at Ved. Stud. i. 170
note.тМЛ

Griffith

Our Father’s Fathers and their sires before them who came, most noble, to the Soma banquet, With these let Yama, yearning with the yearning, rejoicing eat our offerings at his pleasure.

Griffith

Betake thee to the lap of Earth, our mother, of Earth far-spread- ing, very kind and gracious. May she, wool-soft unto the guerdon-giver, guard thee in front upon the distant pathway.

Translation
  1. Swell thou up, O earth; do not press down; be to him easy of access,
    easy of approach; as a mother her son with her skirt (s├нc), do thou, O
    earth (bh┼л╠Бmi), cover him.

b─Бdhith─Бs, in b -va├▒can─Б╠Б, and at end of d bh┼лmi vс╣Ыс╣Зu. We
had the latter hall-verse above, as 2. 50 c, d. The comm.
paraphrases uchva├▒casva with ucch┼лn─Бvayav─Б pulakit─Б bhava. тМКW.
appears to follow the comm. in rendering ├║c chva├▒casva by ‘swell thou
up.’ I do not see why he quit his old version, ‘open thyself.’ In my
Reader, p. 385, I said “Note the meaning of ┼Ыva├▒c [‘open itself;
receive in open arms (as a maid her lover)’] and its concinnity with

Griffith

Heave thyself, Earth, nor press him downward heavily: afford him easy access pleasant to approach, Cover him as a mother wraps her skirt about her child, O Earth!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the earth kindly remain swelling up, for let a thousand props
    support (upa-┼Ыri) it; let these houses, dripping with ghee, pleasant,
    be forever a refuge for him there (├бtra).

Griffith

Now let the heaving earth be free from motion: yea, let a thousand clods remain above him. Be they to him a home distilling fatness: here let them ever be his place of refuge.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I brace up (ut-stabh) the earth from about thee; setting down this
    clod (? log├б), let me take no harm; this pillar do the Fathers
    maintain for thee; let Yama there make seats for thee.
Notes

The corresponding RV. verse (x. 18. 13) reads in c-d dh─Бrayantu t├й
тАШtr─Б тМКp. te ├бtraтМЛ, and ends with minotu. The TA. (in vi. 7. 1)
reads tabhnomi in a тМКdespite the interposition of te: an
interesting variant; cf. Gram. ┬з185 c, aty aс╣гс╣нh─Бt etc.тМЛ; in b,
it substitutes, as do two or three mss. (including our O.) and the
comm., lok├бm тМКsurdтМЛ for log├бm тМКsonant: cf. note to ii. 13. 3тМЛ; at
the juncture of c and d it agrees with RV. тМК-yantu t├й тАШtr─БтМЛ;
and ends with s─Б╠Бdan─Бt te minotu. тМКAs to s─Б╠Бdan─Бt te, cf. the contrary
blunders at xv. 10. 2; xviii. 2. 3, note.тМЛ Nearly all the mss. (all save
our R. and one of SPP’s) have riс╣гan at end of b; but both editions
emend to riс╣гam тМКas RV. readsтМЛ. Our mss. vary in accent between
sth┼лс╣З─Б╠Бm and sth┼л╠Бс╣З─Бс╣Б; in explanation of et─Бс╣Б sth┼лс╣З─Бm, the comm.
says et─Бm prasiddh─Бс╣Б sth┼лс╣З─Бс╣Б tava gс╣Ыhanirm─Бс╣З─Бya. As a triс╣гс╣нubh, the
verse has really three syllables in excess instead of one. K─Бu┼Ы. quotes
it (86. 8) in the ceremony of interment of the bones, with the direction
log─Бn yath─Бparu, doubtless ‘[laying] clods for each several joint’;
the comm. does not notice this.

Griffith

I stay the earth from thee, while over thee I place this piece of earth. May I be free from injury. The Fathers firmly fix this pillar here for thee; and there let Yama make thee an abiding-place.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This bowl, O Agni, do not warp (vi-hvс╣Ы); [it is] dear to the
    gods and the delectable [Fathers]; this bowl here for the gods to
    drink fromтАФin it let the immortal gods revel.
Notes

The RV. has in the corresponding verse (x. 16. 8) eс╣г├б for ay├бm in
c, and at the end m─Бdayante; TA. (in vi. 1. 4) reads in a
j─лhvaras, and, like RV., eс╣г├б in c. The K─Бu┼Ы. (81. 9) makes it
accompany the laying of the iс╕Н─Б-bowl on the head of the corpse on the
funeral pile, when the deceased’s sacrificial implements are disposed
about him to be burned with him. The irregularity of the verse (12 + 11:
10 + 11 = 44) is unnoticed by the Anukr.

Griffith

Forbear, O Agni, to upset this chalice: the Gods and they who merit Soma love it. This cup, yea this which serves the Gods to drink from,–in this let the Immortals take their pleasure.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The bowl that Atharvan bore full to Indra the vigorous, in that he
    makes a draught of what is well done; in that, soma (├нndu) ever
    purifies itself.
Notes

The comm. supplies yaj├▒asya to sukс╣Ыtasya, and, as subject of
kс╣Ыс╣Зoti, с╣Ыtvij─Бс╣Б gaс╣Зaс╕е. тМКThe verse scans as 8 + 12: 11 + 11.тМЛтАФтМКSee my
note on Part VII., above, p. 848.тМЛ

Griffith

The chalice brimming o’er which erst Atharvan offered to Indra, Lord of wealth and treasure, Indu therein sets draught of virtuous action, and ever purifies himself within it.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What of thee the black bird (┼Ыakun├б) thrust at, the ant, the
    serpent, or also the beast of prey (┼Ыv─Б╠Бpada), let the all-eating
    тМКvi┼Ыva-├бdтМЛ Agni make that free from disease, and the soma that hath
    entered the Brahmans.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 16. 6 without variant. TA. has it also, in vi. 4. 2.
TA. reads in c тМКfor vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бd (‘all-consuming’) agad├бm, the
curiously pervertedтМЛ v├н┼Ыv─Бd (‘from every’) anс╣Ыс╣З├бm тМКwhich is glossed
by sarvasm─Бd upadrav─Бd с╣Ыс╣Зarahitam upadravarahitamтМЛ. In d it has
br─Бhmaс╣З├бm (also, in the printed тМКCalc.тМЛ text, ─Бviv├н┼Ыeс╣гa; but its
comm. тМКCalc.тМЛ explains br─Бhmaс╣Зe and ─Бvive┼Ыa); тМКin the Poona ed. the
comm. seems to show an alternative reading, either br─Бhmaс╣Зe or
br─Бhmaс╣Зam, glossed by etad─лye br─Бhmaс╣Зa┼Ыar─лre; and it reads of course
─Бvive┼ЫaтМЛ. тМКOur prat─лka is cited by Ke┼Ыava, p. 368┬╣тБ░, as yat te
kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зaс╕е ┼Ыakun─лty с╣Ыc─Б: is ┼Ыakun─л a blunder? cf. id├бс╣Б y├бt kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З├бс╕е
┼Ыak├║nis, vii. 64. 1, 2.тМЛ

In K─Бu┼Ы. the verse is used (80. 5) in the very introduction of the
adhy─Бya, before the handling of the corpse begins; and Ke┼Ыava says it
is in case the man dies of the bite of a crow or ant or the like; the
comm. makes the same condition, and adds that the wounded place is to be
burned with fire; this is then probably the meaning of K─Бu┼Ыika’s
direction ity avad─лpayati. The verse appears again (83. 20) in
connection with the strewing and covering of the bone-relics.

Griffith

What wound soe’er the dark bird hath inflicted, the emmet, or the serpent, or the jackal, May Agni who devoureth all things heal it, and Soma, who hath passed into the Brahmans.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрджрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╖реИрд▓рд╛ рдкрдХреНрд╖реА, рдкрд╢реБ, рд╕рд░реНрдк, рдХреАрдЯ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХрд╛рдЯ рдЦрд╛рд╡реЗ, рддреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдереЛрдбрд╝реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖реИрд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рдХрд╛рдЯреЗ рдХреЛ рдЖрдЧ рд╕реЗ рд╕реЗрдХ рджреЗрдВрдФрд░ рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖реИрд▓реЗ рдХреЗ рдХрд╛рдЯреЗ рдХреЛ рдЖрдЧ рд╕реЗ рдЬрд▓рд╛рд╡реЗрдВ рддрдерд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡реИрджреНрдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рднреА рдФрд╖рдзрдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗрдВ, рдпрд╣ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерелрелреердпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ рд╣реИтИТрезрежредрезремредремрее

Translation
  1. Rich in milk are the herbs; rich in milk is my milk; what is the
    milk of the milk of the waters, therewith let one beautify (┼Ыubh) me.
Notes

тМКThe translation implies (instead of the ┼Ыumbhantu of the Berlin text)
the reading ┼Ыumbhatu, which is read by most of SPP’s authorities and
some of W’s and adopted by SPP. Two or three of SPP’s, and W’s Op., have
┼Ыumbhata (a blend of AV. ┼Ыumbhatu and RV. ┼Ыundhata?). For the
misuse of ┼Ыumbh for ┼Ыundh, see note to vi. 115. 3.тМЛ The
corresponding verse in RV. is x. 17. 14, which has v├бcas instead of
p├бyas at end of b; for c, the less repetitious ap─Б╠Бm p├бyasvad
├нt p├бyaс╕е, and at the end ┼Ыundhata. TS. (in i. 5. 10┬▓) and TB. (in
iii. 7. 4тБ╖) have again a quite different version: namely, for b,
p├бyasvad v─лrudh─Бm p├бyaс╕е; for c, our c; for d, t├йna m─Б╠Бm
indra s├бс╣Б sс╣Ыja. Ppp. also has the verse тМКin xx.тМЛ with vacas in b.
Its former half appeared above, as iii. 24. 1 a, b, likewise with
v├бcas. In K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 9), it is used in the ceremonies of the first day
after cremation, with strewing tufts of ku┼Ыa-grass; the comm.,
however, says instead that it accompanies a bath taken immediately after
the cremation of the dead body. The comm. supplies Varuс╣Зa, as god of the
waters, for subject of the concluding verb.

Griffith

The plants of earth are rich in milk, and rich in milk is this my milk. With all the milky essence of the Waters let them make me clean.

Griffith

Let these unwidowed dames with goodly husbands adorn them- selves with fragrant balm and unguent. Decked with fair jewels, tearless, free, from trouble, first let the dames go up to where he lieth.

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реА рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдБрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рд╢реБрдн рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕реБрдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдХреБрдЯреБрдореНрдмрд┐рдпреЛрдВрдкрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдФрд░ рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдФрд░ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрде рд░рд╣рдХрд░ рдмрд╣реБрдд рдзрдирд╡рддреА рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдЦрд╡рддреАрд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЕрдЧреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдиреА рдмрдирддреА рд╣реИрдВ реерелренреердпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХреБрдЫ рднреЗрдж рд╕реЗ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ рд╣реИтИТрезрежредрезреоредренред рдФрд░рдКрдкрд░ рдЖрдЪреБрдХрд╛ рд╣реИ-рдЕреж резреиредреиредрейрез рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. Unite thyself (sam-gam) with the Fathers, with Yama, with thy
    sacred and charitable works in the highest firmament; abandoning what is
    reproachful, come again home;тАФlet him unite himself with a body, very
    splendid.
Notes

The corresponding verse in RV. (x. 14. 8) reads in c hitv─Б╠Бya, and
in d gachasva, continuing the general construction of the verse. The
first half is found also in TA. (in vi. 4. 2), which has svadh─Б╠Бbhis
for yam├йna, and adds after it another s├бm. We had the last p─Бda
above, as 2. 10 d. The mss. are divided between ├бvadyam and
avady├бm in c; both editions give avady├бm тМКwith RV.тМЛ.

Griffith

Meet Yama, meet the Fathers, meet the merit of virtuous action in the loftiest heaven. Leave sin and evil, seek anew thy dwelling: so bright with glory let him join his body.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - [рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп !] (рдпрдореЗрдирд╕рдореН) рдирд┐рдпрдо [рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рд╡реНрд░рдд] рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдкреВрд░реНрддреЗрди) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ, рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрди рддрдерд╛рдЕрдиреНрдирджрд╛рди рдЖрджрд┐ рдкреБрдгреНрдп рдХрд░реНрдо рд╕реЗ (рдкрд░рдореЗ) рд╕рдмрд╕реЗ рдКрдБрдЪреЗ (рд╡реНрдпреЛрдордиреН) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдкрдж рдореЗрдВ [рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рди] (рдкрд┐рддреГрднрд┐рдГ) рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВ [рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рдорд╣рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ] рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╕реНрд╡) рддреВ рдорд┐рд▓ред (рдЕрд╡рджреНрдпрдореН)рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░реНрдо [рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди] рдХреЛ (рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛) рдЫреЛрдбрд╝рдХрд░ (рдкреБрдирдГ) рдлрд┐рд░ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрдореН) рдШрд░ (рдЖ рдЗрд╣рд┐) рддреВ рдЖрдФрд░ (рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдЪрд╛рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рд╣реЛрдХрд░ (рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛) рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рд╕рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд╛рдореН) рдЖрдкрдорд┐рд▓реЗрдВ реерелреорее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрдЪрд┐рдд рд╣реИрдХрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рддрдк рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдорд╣рд╛рд╢рдпреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗрдЧреГрд╣рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдо рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реЗрд╢ рдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкреА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерелреореердпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХреБрдЫ рднреЗрдж рд╕реЗ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ рд╣реИтИТрезрежредрезрекредреоред рдФрд░ рдЗрд╕ рдХрд╛ рдЪреМрдерд╛ рдкрд╛рдж рдКрдкрд░ рдЖрдЪреБрдХрд╛ рд╣реИ-рдЕреж резреоредреиредрезрежред рддрдерд╛ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрдкрд╛рда рдорд╣рд░реНрд╖рд┐рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдХреГрдд рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд░рдг рдореЗрдВ рдЙрджреНрдзреГрдд рд╣реИ рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: релреотИТ(рд╕рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╕реНрд╡)рд╕рдВрдЧрддреЛ рднрд╡ (рдкрд┐рддреГрднрд┐рдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХреИрд░реНрдорд╣рд╛рддреНрдорднрд┐рдГ (рд╕рдореН) рд╕рд╣ (рдпрдореЗрди) рдирд┐рдпрдореЗрдиредрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрд░рддреЗрди (рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдкреВрд░реНрддреЗрди) рдЕреж реиредрезреиредрекред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╡реЗрджрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╛рдиреНрдирджрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛ (рдкрд░рдореЗ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ (рд╡реНрдпреЛрдордиреН) рдЕреж резредрезренредремред рд╡рд┐+рдЕрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗ-рдордирд┐рдиреНред рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдкрджреЗ (рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреНрдпрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ (рдЕрд╡рджреНрдпрдореН) рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рдкреБрдирдГ) рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрддрдореН) рдЧреГрд╣рдореН (рдПрд╣рд┐) рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ (рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд╛рдореН) рд╕рдВрдЧрддреЛ рднрд╡рддреБ рднрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рддрдиреНрд╡рд╛) рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд╢рдХреНрддреНрдпрд╛ (рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдЪрд╛рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рее

Whitney
Translation
  1. They that are our father’s fathers, that are [his] grandfathers,
    that entered the wide atmosphereтАФfor them may the autocratic (svar─Б╠Бj)
    second life today shape our bodies as he will.
Notes

The first half-verse we had above as 2. 49 a, b тМКand its prior p─Бda
also at 3. 46тМЛ; the second half-verse corresponds to the second half of
RV. x. 15. 14 (and VS. xix. 60), but is much corrupted, even to
unintelligibility, so that the translation is only mechanical. RV. reads
t├йbhiс╕е svar─Б╠Бс╕Н ├бsun─лtim et─Б╠Бс╣Б yath─Бva┼Ы├бс╣Б tanv├ас╣Б kalpayasva; VS. has
t├йbhyas and kalpay─Бti, but the rest like RV. The last p─Бda is
identical with vii. 104. 1 d above.

Griffith

Our Father’s Fathers and their sires before them, they who have entered into air’s wide region, For them shall self-resplendent Asuniti form bodies now accord- ing to her pleasure.

ремреж рд╢рдВ рддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the mist be weal for thee; let the frost fall down [as] weal
    for thee; O cool one, possessing cool ones; O refreshing one, possessing
    refreshing ones; mayest thou be with weal a she-frog in the waters;
    kindly pacify thou this fire.
Notes

Or, ’this Agni.’тАФOf the ritual use of this verse, the comm. simply says
that with it one is to sprinkle the bones of a Brahman with the plants
referred to, dipped in water and milk; K─Бu┼Ы. (82. 26) combines it with
3. 5 тМКdoubtless rather 3. 5 and 6: see under 3. 5тМЛ, in the manner
explained under that verse. тМКPartly because W. overlooked some TA.
variants, it seemed necessary for me to rewrite the next paragraph; but
I could not easily indicate my changes and additions by the usual
ell-brackets.тМЛ

The main stock of this verse (p─Бdas c-f) is RV. x. 16. 14 and is the
third verse of TA. vi. 4. 1: in both these texts it stands next after
the verse which corresponds to our 3. 6 above, namely after RV. x. 16.
13 = TA. vi. 4. 1┬▓: see note to 3. 6. Considering how closely it is
connected with our 3. 6 in sense and in position in those texts, it is
strange that it should be so removed from 3. 6 in AV.тАФIn d part of
the mss. (including our Bp.P.M.I.: also the comm.) read hl─Б╠Бdake
hl─Б╠Бdak-; TA. has hl─Б╠Бduke hl─Б╠Бduk-. For e, RV. has maс╣Зс╕Н┼лky├а s├║ s├бс╣Б
gamaс╕е (of which our version, p. maс╣Зс╕Н┼лk─л╠Б: apре░s├║: ┼Ы├бm: bhuvaс╕е, is no
better than a corruption), and TA., again differently, maс╣Зс╕Н┼лky├аsu (as
an adjective, supplying apsu) saс╣Бgam├бya; and the comm., finally,
maс╣Зс╕Н┼лky─Б тАЩsya ┼Ыam bhava: moreover, for the ┼Ы├бm of both ed’s, some of
our mss. (O.Op.R.) and one of SPP’s have s├бm. In e, at the end,
RV. has harс╣гaya and TA. ┼Ыam├бya: our ┼Ыamaya is better than
either.тАФTo the main stock of the AV. verse are prefixed two p─Бdas which
agree nearly with the second half of the next verse but one in TA. (vs.
5: interposed as vs. 4 is matter that corresponds to our i. 6. 4 and
xix. 2. 1, 2): but for our bhavatu the TA. has varс╣гatu; and for our
┼Ы├бс╣Б te pruс╣гv─Б╠Б, it has ┼Ы├бm u pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣нh─Б (so Calc.: the Poona ed. accepts
pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гv─Б but gives pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh─Б as variant): the comm. glosses pс╣Ыс╣гv─Б with
jalabinduс╕е,тАФFor Bloomfield’s discussion, see under vs. 6. Bergaigne
comments on the verse, Rel. V├йd. i. 84, note, ii. 472.

Griffith

Let the hoar-frost be sweet to thee. sweetly on thee the rain descend! O full of coolness, thou cool Plant, full of fresh moisture, fresh- ening Herb, Bless us in waters, female Frog: calm and allay this Agni here.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Vivasvant make for us freedom from fear, he who is
    well-preserving, quick-giving (? -d─Б╠Бnu), well-giving; let these heroes
    be many here; let there be in me prosperity (puс╣гс╣н├б) rich in kine, rich
    in horses.

kart─Б and vayoh─Бner (as if from jс╣Ы ‘waste away’) d─Бt─Б. тМКP─Бda

Griffith

Vivasvan make us free from fear and peril, good rescuer, quick- pouring, bounteous giver! Many in number be these present heroes! Increase of wealth be mine in kine and horses!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Vivasvant set us in immortality; let death go away; let what is
    immortal come to us; let [him] defend these men until old age; let not
    their life-breaths (├бsu) go to Yama.
Notes

In ┼Ы┼ЫS. iv. 16. 5, and MB. i. 1. 15 are found as the first two p─Бdas of
a verse our 62 b and 61 a. тМКFor the na ─Бitu of our 62 b,
both texts have ma ─Б g─Бt (the me is incongruent with the following
nas*);* and for the vivasv─Бn of our 61 a, both have vaivasvato,тМЛ
thus rectifying the meter. The mss. accent vivasv─Бn as in 61 a. We
need to resolve m├│ to m─Б╠Б u in d to make a good triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda;
but the Anukr. would apparently read mo and balance the lack of a
syllable by the redundancy of one in c. Possibly ─Б╠Б is intrusive in
c, and the meaning was ‘defend from growing old.’ The ritual use of
the verse was explained above, under vs. 61.

Griffith

In immortality Vivasvan set us! Go from us Death, come to us life eternal! To good old age may he protect these people: let not their spirits pass away to Yama.

Translation

63 . He who maintains himself by his might, like [birds?] in the
atmosphere, poet of the Fathers, favorer (? pr├бmati) of prayers
(mat├н)тАФhim praise ye, all-befriended, with oblations; may that Yama
give (dh─Б) us to live further on.

Notes

The reading in the first p─Бda is doubtful; our text has ant├бrikс╣гeс╣Зa,
but the other edition -kс╣гe n├б. Bp. and Op. read ant├бrikс╣гe: n├б, and
so, apparently, SPP’s pada-mss. but our D.K. have -kс╣гeс╣Зa, and with
it agree our P.M.I., while O.R.T., though they give na, do not accent
it; SPP’s mss. are somewhat similarly at variance. The commentator’s
interpretation is an interpretation of antarikс╣гeс╣Зa; but his text
(according to SPP.) reads -kс╣гe na. Only the sense can decide, and that
is quite doubtful; the translation ventured above implies -kс╣гe n├б. The
second half-verse occurs again below as 4. 54 c, d. One is tempted
to understand vi┼Ыv├бmitr─Бs тМКso accented in both ed’s with all the
authoritiesтМЛ in c as ‘O Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras’; but this is so decidedly
opposed by the accent and by the short vowel of the second syllable
(which is authenticated by the pada-reading vi┼Ыv├бре░mitr─Бс╕е, while
vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бmitra is never divided: see Pr─Бt. iii. 9 and note) that I have
not dared to assume it; тМКbut the comm., ignoring these considerations,
takes it as voc. For the verse in general,тМЛ the comm., as usual in a
trying case, gives no help whatever; he glosses pramati with
prakс╣Ыс╣гс╣нabuddhi, and mati with mantс╣Ы or stotс╣Ы, in apposition with
pitс╣Эс╣З─Бm; and he makes antarikс╣гeс╣Зa dadhre mean (pitс╣Эn) antar─Б
kс╣г─Бntena lokena dh─Бrayati.

Griffith

The Sage of Fathers, guardian of devotions who holds thee up with might in air’s mid-region,– Praise him ye Visvamitras, with oblation. To lengthened life shall be, this Yama, lead us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ascend ye to the highest heaven; O seers, be not afraid; ye
    soma-drinkers, soma-drenchers, this oblation is made to you; we have
    gone to the highest light.
Notes

Encouraged by the comm. (any─Бn api yajam─Бn─Бn somam p─Бyayanti), the
translation mends the repetition in c by violently taking -p─Бyin
as causative to -p─Б.

Griffith

Mount and ascend to highest heaven, O Rishis: be ye not afraid. Soma-drinkers to you is paid this Soma-lover’s sacrifice. We have attained the loftiest light.

Translation
  1. Agni shines forth with great show (ket├║); the bull roars loudly
    unto the two firmaments (r├│das─л); тМКevenтМЛ from the end of heaven he
    hath attained unto me (?); in the lap of the waters the buffalo
    increased.

Griffith

Agni is shining forth with lofty banner: the Bull is bellowing to earth and heaven. From the sky’s limit even hath he stretched near us: the Steer hath waxen in the waters’ bosom.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As, longing with the heart, they looked upon thee, flying up*
    [as] an eagle in the firmament (n─Б╠Бka), golden-winged messenger of
    Varuс╣Зa, busy (bhuraс╣Зy├║) bird (┼Ыakun├б) in the lair of Yama.
Notes

The RV. has the verse (x. 123. 6), and it is found also in SV. (i. 320
and ii. 1196), TB. (in ii. 5. 8тБ╡), and TA. (vi. 3. 1); all read alike
throughout, save that the RV. (not the SV.) pada-text has the bad
division and accent abh├н: ├бcakс╣гata. Our P.M.O. have at the end
bhuraс╣Зy├бm. It is noteworthy that vss. 65 and 66, which have no
apparent connection with funeral rites, and are not used by K─Бu┼Ы. save
in the group 61-67, are found almost together (separated only by our 3.
7) also in the funeral collection of TA. *тМКW’s “up” for ├║pa may be an
oversight: render perhaps ’they looked upon thee, flying onward (├║pa)
[as] an eagle’? Our comm., taking ’thee’ as the dead man, construes,
‘flying unto the eagle’; but is not the verse addressed rather to Agni?
cf. Griffith and comm. on TA.тАФS─Бyaс╣Зa, commenting on the RV. vs., says
he vena; but in his comm. on TB. he says he pravargyasv─Бmin: an
interesting diversity of opinion! Perhaps RV. ix. 85. 11 may throw light
on our verse.тМЛ

Griffith

They gaze on thee with longing in their spirit, as on an eagle that is mounting skyward; On thee with wings of gold, Varuna’s envoy, the Bird that hasteth to the home of Yama.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Indra, bring us ability (kr├бtu), as a father to his sons; help
    (┼Ыikс╣г) us in this course (y─Б╠Бman), O much-invoked one; may we,
    living, attain to light.
Notes

The verse is RV. vii. 32. 26, found also as SV. i. 259; ii. 806, and TS.
vii. 5. 7тБ┤; the only variant anywhere is that TS. has no as-,
unlingualized, in c. The comm. glosses y─Б╠Бmani with
saс╣Бs─Бragamane, and ┼Ы├нkс╣гa by anu┼Ы─Бdhi.

Griffith

O Indra, bring us wisdom as a sire gives wisdom to his sons. Guide us, O much-invoked in this our way: may we still living look upon the Sun.

Griffith

Let these which Gods have held for thee, the beakers covered o’er with cake, Be full of sacred food for thee, distilling fatness, rich in mead.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What grains I scatter along for thee, mixed with sesame, rich in
    svadh─Б╠Б, be they for thee abundant (vibh├║), prevailing; them let king
    Yama approve for thee.
Notes

According to the comm., the grains are roasted barley; and anu
manyat─Бm means ‘assent to thine enjoying’; тМКat 4. 26 he says t─Б dh─Бn─Бs
tava bhog─Бya…anuj─Бn─Бtu. It depends on Yama’s favor, says Weber,
Sb., 1896, p. 276, whether the dead man may have the benefit of his
viaticum, or not.тМЛ The verse is nearly identical with 4. 26, and is
precisely identical with 4. 43. Its meter is (9 + 8: 8 + 10 = 35) rather
irregular, and lacks a syllable of being full measure. тМКWith an easy
double sandhi in a (dh─Бn─Бnu-) and the resolutions ta─Бs and r─Бj─Б
anu in d, it scans very well as 8 + 8: 8 + 12.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. (85. 27)
directs that grains be scattered ‘with verses that have the sign
(salin╠Дga)’; and Ke┼Ыava states these verses to be the two that begin
y─Бs te dh─Бn─Бs (doubtless 3. 69 тМК= 4. 43тМЛ and 4. 26, since 3. 70 is
evidently not salin╠Дga), also 4. 32 and 33, and another not found in
the text; the comm. says that such grains are to be put upon the bones
with the two vss. that begin with y─Бs te dh─Бnas, тМКby which he seems to
mean 3. 69 (= 4. 43) and 4. 26 rather than 3. 69 and 70: at any rate, he
immediately cites 3. 70 for another useтМЛ.

тМКIt is hardly doubtful that the black variety of sesame (kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зatila) is
meant here, and that it is used, like the black rice and black victim,
on account of its color: Pischel, GGA., 1897, p. 813. Pischel’s view is
confirmed by the fact that, if an offering to the Manes is performed
apropos of some joyful occurrence in the family, barley is substituted
for sesame: so ┼Ыr─Бddhakalpa, iv. 5, as cited by Caland,
Totenverehrung, p. 37.тМЛ

Griffith

Grains which for thee I scatter, mixt with Sesamum, as holy food, May they for thee be excellent and potent: King Yama look on them as thine with favour!

Whitney
Translation
  1. Give back, O forest tree, him who is deposited here with thee, that
    in Yama’s seat he may sit speaking counsels.
Notes

Two of our pada-mss. (Bp.Kp.) read vid├бtha in d. The verse is
repeated, according to K─Бu┼Ы. (83. 19), when the bone-relics are removed
from the root of a tree, at which they had been for some time deposited:
the comm. adds “provided they have been previously so deposited.” It
reads more as if it were originally addressed to the (hollowed) tree in
which a corpse is buried (in which case, tv├бyi ought to be rendered
‘in thee’). тМКWith regard to vanaspate, see my note to 2. 25, above:
and as to vid├бth─Б, see Geldner, ZDMG. lii. 735.тМЛ

Griffith

O Tree, give back again this man who is deposited on thee. That he may dwell in Yama’s home addressing the assemblies there.

Translation
  1. Take hold, O J─Бtavedas; let thy seizure (h├бras) be with sharpness
    (t├йjas-); his body do thou consume; then set him in the world of the
    well-doing.
Notes

with 2.4 and others (see under 2. 4) at the lighting of the funeral
pile.

Griffith

Seize hold O Jatavedas; let thy flame be full of fervent heat. Consume his body: to the world of pious ones transport this man.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What Fathers of thine went away earlier and what later, for them let
    there go a brook of ghee, hundred-streamed, overflowing.
Notes

The second half of the verse is nearly identical with 4. 57 c, d
below. The mss. are not agreed about kuly─Б├м тАЩtu тМКso both ed’sтМЛ: some
(including our R. and тМКone orтМЛ two of SPP’s) read kuly├и тАЩta. Our Bp.
has kuly─Б╠А: etu; but Op. accents -y─Б╠Б, and Kp. has kulyaре░etu. The
noun is elsewhere accented kuly─Б╠Б, and hence our text ought doubtless
to he kuly─Б├н тАЩtu тМКso SPP’s B.тМЛ. The verse is twice used with 4. 57 in
K─Бu┼Ы.: once (86. 2) in the ceremony of interment of the bones, on
filling a dish (caru) with butter and honey and depositing it by the
head тМКsee note to 4. 16тМЛ; and again (88. 17), in the piс╣Зс╕Нapitс╣Ыyaj├▒a,
on smearing the piс╣Зс╕Нas with sacrificial butter.

Griffith

To these, thy Fathers who have passed away at first and after- ward, Let the full brook of butter run, o’erflowing with a hundred streams.

unmс╣Ыj─Бnas as ┼Ыar─лr─Бd utkramaс╣Зena sv─Бtm─Бnaс╣Б ┼Ыodhayan. For the use of
the verse in K─Бu┼Ы. 85. 24, with 2. 37, see under the latter. тМКCf. p.
848, ┬╢8.тМЛ

тМКHere ends the third anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 73 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says saptatis tryadhik─Б paraс╕е: cf. page 814.тМЛ

Griffith

Mount to this life, removing all defilement: here thine own kindred shine with lofty splendour. Depart thou; be not left behind: go forward, first of those here, unto the world of Fathers.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - [рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп !] (рдПрддрддреН)рдЗрд╕ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЛ (рдЙрдиреНрдореГрдЬрд╛рдирдГ) рд╢реБрджреНрдз рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рддреВ (рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣) рдКрдБрдЪрд╛ рдЪрдврд╝, (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдмрд╛рдиреНрдзрд╡ рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдЗрд╣) рдпрд╣рд╛рдБ рдкрд░ (рдмреГрд╣рддреН) рдмрд╣реБрдд (рд╣рд┐) рд╣реА (рджреАрджрдпрдиреНрддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╣реИрдВред рддреВ (рдЕрднрд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ (рдкреНрд░) рдЖрдЧреЗ рдХреЛ (рдЗрд╣рд┐) рдЪрд▓, (рдордзреНрдпрддрдГ) рдмреАрдЪ рд╕реЗ (рдкрд┐рддреДрдгрд╛рдореН) рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдВрдХреЗ (рд▓реЛрдХрдореН) рдЙрд╕ рд╕рдорд╛рдЬ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдк) рдмрд┐рд▓рдЧрд╛ рдХрд░ (рдорд╛ рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдГ) рдордд рдЬрд╛, (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ [рд╕рдорд╛рдЬ] (рдЕрддреНрд░)рдпрд╣рд╛рдБ рдкрд░ (рдкреНрд░рдердордГ) рдореБрдЦреНрдп рд╣реИ рееренрейрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдпрд╢рд╕реНрд╡реАрдмрд╛рдиреНрдзрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЕрдкрдирд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рди рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдмрдирд╛рд╡реЗрдВ, рдФрд░ рд╕рдм рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрда рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреГрдврд╝рддрд╛ рд╕реЗрдЖрд░рдореНрдн рдХрд░ рдХреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░ рдорд╣рд╛рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдкрд╛рд╡реЗрдВ рееренрейрее рдЗрддрд┐рддреГрддреАрдпреЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: ренрейтИТ(рдПрддрддреН) рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣) рдЖрд░реБрд╣реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН (рдЙрдиреНрдореГрдЬрд╛рдирдГ) рдкрд░рд┐рд╢реЛрдзрдпрдиреН (рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрдпрдГ (рдЗрд╣) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд▓реНрд▓реЛрдХреЗ (рдмреГрд╣рддреН) рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛редрдЕрдзрд┐рдХрдореН (рджреАрджрдпрдиреНрддреЗ) рджреАрджрдпрддрд┐рд░реНрдЬреНрд╡рд▓рддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ рдирд┐рдШреж резредрезремред рджреАрджрдпрддрд┐рд░реНрдиреИрд░реБрдХреНрддреЛ рдзрд╛рддреБрдГ-рдкрд╢реНрдпрддрдирд┐рд░реБреж резрежредрезрепред рджреАрдкреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ (рдЕрднрд┐) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдГ (рдкреНрд░) рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рдЕрдЧреНрд░реЗ (рдЗрд╣рд┐) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ (рдордзреНрдпрддрдГ)рдордзреНрдпрднрд╛рдЧрд╛рддреН (рдЕрдк) рдЕрдкреЗрддреНрдп рд╡рд┐рдпреБрдЬреНрдп (рдорд╛ рд╣рд╛рд╕реНрдерд╛рдГ) рдУрд╣рд╛рдЩреН рдЧрддреМ-рд▓реБрдЩреНред рдорд╛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫ (рдкрд┐рддреДрдгрд╛рдореН) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдореНред (рд▓реЛрдХрдореН) рд╕рдорд╛рдЬрдореН (рдкреНрд░рдердордГ) рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдГ (рдпрдГ) рд▓реЛрдХрдГ (рдЕрддреНрд░) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рее
